{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01NMLnNaP68b2K2VFkBMxxxw","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"You know what, let me take a step back and look at this from first principles. Let me examine what the comparison operator should logically be. Currently it's `>=`. Let me think about whether it should be `>`:\n\nWhen `CONN_MAX_AGE = 0`:\n- `close_at = time.monotonic()` (at the exact moment connect() is called, let's call this T0)\n- Later, `close_if_unusable_or_obsolete()` is called at time T1\n- With `>=`: if T1 >= T0 (which is almost always true), close the connection\n- With `>`: if T1 > T0 (which is almost always true), close the connection\n\nSo both would have the same effect in practice.\n\nBut wait! What if the issue is that the check should use `>` to be consistent with the concept of \"exceeding\" a time? Let me look at the docstring again: \"if it outlived its maximum age\". True at or after N seconds -> connection closed at or after N seconds ✓\n\nBoth seem to work correctly! But there's a subtle difference in the timing. With `>`, there's a guarantee that SOME time passes before closing. With `>=`, the connection could close at the exact boundary.\n\nHmm, actually, I think I might have found it!
